<div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">CLASH: DISCOVERY OF A BRIGHT <I>z</I> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 6.2 DWARF GALAXY QUADRUPLY LENSED BY MACS J0329.6-0211</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">A. class=\"icon-arrow-down\"></span></a>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"nav-drop-down\" data-nav-item=\"table\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"overflow-x\" class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">2041-8205/747/1/L9</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n                      <P>We report the discovery of a <I>z</I>             <SUB>phot</SUB> = 6.18<SUP>+0.05</SUP>             <SUB>\u2013 0.07</SUB> (95% confidence level) dwarf galaxy, lensed into four images by the galaxy cluster MACS J0329.6-0211 (<I>z<SUB>l</SUB>             </I> = 0.45). The galaxy is observed as a high-redshift dropout in <I>HST</I>/ACS/WFC3 CLASH and <I>Spitzer</I>/IRAC imaging. Its redshift is securely determined due to a clear detection of the Lyman break in the 18-band photometry, making this galaxy one of the highest-redshift multiply lensed objects known to date with an observed magnitude of F125W =24.00 \u00b1 0.04 AB mag for its most magnified image. We also present the first strong-lensing analysis of this cluster uncovering 15 additional multiply imaged candidates of five lower-redshift sources spanning the range <I>z<SUB>s</SUB>             </I> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 2-4. The mass model independently supports the high photometric redshift and reveals magnifications of 11.6<SUP>+8.9</SUP>             <SUB>\u2013 4.1</SUB>, 17.6<SUP>+6.2</SUP>             <SUB>\u2013 3.9</SUB>, 3.9<SUP>+3.0</SUP>             <SUB>\u2013 1.7</SUB>, and 3.7<SUP>+1.3</SUP>             <SUB>\u2013 0.2</SUB>, respectively, for the four images of the high-redshift galaxy. By delensing the most magnified image we construct an image of the source with a physical resolution of ~200 pc when the universe was ~0.9\u00a0Gyr old, where the <I>z</I> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 6.2 galaxy occupies a source-plane area of approximately 2.2\u00a0kpc<SUP>2</SUP>. Modeling the observed spectral energy distribution using population synthesis models, we find a demagnified stellar mass of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"${\\sim}10^{9} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/apjl421305ieqn1.gif\"></IMG>, subsolar metallicity (<I>Z</I>/<I>Z</I>             <SUB>\u2609</SUB> ~ 0.5), low dust content (<I>A<SUB>V</SUB>             </I> ~ 0.1\u00a0mag), a demagnified star formation rate (SFR) of <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"${\\sim}3.2 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/apjl421305ieqn2.gif\"></IMG> yr<SUP>\u20131</SUP>, and a specific SFR of ~3.4\u00a0Gyr<SUP>\u20131</SUP>, all consistent with the properties of local dwarf galaxies.</P>       </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/747/1/L9&doi=10.1088/2041-8205/747/1/L9&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/747/1/L9&doi=10.1088/2041-8205/747/1/L9&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2012ApJ...747L...9Z\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2012ApJ...747L...9Z&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2012ApJ...747L...9Z\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/2041-8205/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl421305s1\" name=\"apjl421305s1\">1.\u00a0INTRODUCTION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>By gravitationally lensing distant background sources, galaxy clusters act as natural magnifying lenses in the sky, providing a unique window into the early universe. Several high-redshift galaxies have been discovered through the magnification power of galaxy clusters (e.g., Franx et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r22\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r22\">1997</a>; Frye et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r23\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r23\">2002</a>; Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r7\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r7\">2009a</a>; Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r44\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r44\">2009</a>; Bradley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r11\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r11\">2011</a>). The current highest-redshift lensed galaxy is at <em>z</em> = 7.6 in the field of A1689 (Bradley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r10\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r10\">2008</a>), but among the highest-redshift <em>multiply lensed</em> galaxies known are a galaxy at <em>z</em> = 6.03 in the field of A383 (comprising two images; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r40\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r40\">2011</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r47\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r47\">2011c</a>), a <em>z</em> ~ 6.5 galaxy in the field of A2218 (comprising three images; Kneib et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r29\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r29\">2004</a>; Egami et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r20\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r20\">2005</a>), and a <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidate in the \"bullet cluster\" (comprising two images; Hall et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r25\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r25\">2012</a>). In addition, the lens model can be used to map the lensed images back into the source plane, while the high magnification enables their spatially resolved internal structural properties to be measured. Such measurements are not possible without the aid of the lensing power of the cluster (e.g., Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r46\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r46\">2011b</a>).</p><p>The Ly\u03b1 forest produces a sharp drop in flux below 1216\u2009\u00c5. The expansion of the universe moves this spectral break to longer wavelengths, allowing high-redshift galaxies to be identified as \"dropouts\" in the observed-frame optical and near-IR (see Madau <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r32\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r32\">1995</a>; Franx et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r22\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r22\">1997</a>). As these young, high-redshift galaxies are usually actively forming stars, their rest-frame UV spectra should be relatively blue. This combination of properties allows the redshift of the galaxy to be estimated accurately, even without spectroscopy: as low as ~1% uncertainty on the redshift is obtained here, for 95% confidence levels. The study of high-redshift galaxies enables important constraints to be placed on galaxy evolution and structure formation. Particularly, observing high-redshift galaxies provides direct measurements of the high-<em>z</em> luminosity function, early star formation rate (SFR), and the epoch of the intergalactic medium reionization (see Bradley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r11\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r11\">2011</a> and references therein).</p><p>We report the discovery of one of the highest-redshift (<em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> = 6.18<sup>+0.05</sup><sub>\u2212 0.07</sub>) multiply lensed galaxies known to date, lensed into four images by the galaxy cluster MACS J0329.6-0211 (<em>z</em> = 0.45; MACS0329 hereafter). MACS0329 is an X-ray-selected system found by the Massive Cluster Survey (MACS; Ebeling et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r18\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r18\">2001</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r19\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r19\">2010</a>). Maughan et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r34\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r34\">2008</a>) classified MACS0329 as having evidence for substructure in its X-ray surface brightness, although Schmidt &amp; Allen (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r41\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r41\">2007</a>) classified it as relaxed. We found no record of previous strong-lensing (SL) analysis of this cluster, and only one-band shallow <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>)/WFPC2 previous imaging. The 16 <em>HST</em> bands chosen for the Cluster Lensing and Supernova survey with Hubble (CLASH; Postman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r39\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r39\">2012</a>) enable us to conduct the first SL study of this cluster, and to obtain accurate photometric redshifts for the multiply lensed background galaxies. We use these data in conjunction with a parametric SL modeling method (e.g., Broadhurst et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r12\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r12\">2005</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r48\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r48\">2009</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r45\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r45\">2011a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r46\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r46\">2011b</a>; Merten et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r36\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r36\">2011</a>), to find several multiple image families across the central field of MACS0329 (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f1\">1</a>) so that its mass distribution and inner profile can be well constrained, allowing us to deduce the source-plane properties of the high-redshift galaxy presented here.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl421305f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl421305f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Galaxy cluster MACS0329 (<em>z</em> = 0.45) imaged with <em>HST</em>/ACS/WFC3. We number the multiple images uncovered by our model, where the two candidate systems are marked in \"c.\" All systems are accurately reproduced by our model, with an average image-plane reproduction uncertainty of 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />07 per image, and image-plane <em>rms</em> of 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />32, excluding candidate systems. The white critical curve corresponds to system 1 at <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 6.18 and the blue critical curve corresponds to system 2 at <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 2.17. The composition of this color image is red = F105W+F110W+F125W+F140W+F160W, green = F606W+F625W+F775W+F814W+F850LP, and blue = F435W+F475W. The upper-right inset shows a blow-up of the <em>z</em> = 6.18 system, below which we inset the source galaxy reproduced by our model, by delensing the most magnified image 1.2 (\u03bc ~ 17.6) to the source plane, yielding a resolution of ~200 pc pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>. Overplotted therein are bars showing the source-plane size of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2 (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 1.2\u00a0kpc). Noise cleaning and color manipulation procedures were performed for a better view of the internal details of the source.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjl421305f1\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadFigure/figure/apjl421305f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl421305f1\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl421305f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The Letter is organized as follows. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjl421305s2\">2</a> we describe the observations, and in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjl421305s3\">3</a> we detail the SL model. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjl421305s4\">4</a>, we report the results of the SL analysis and the physical properties of the high-redshift galaxy based on detailed spectral energy distribution (SED) modeling. The results and conclusions are summarized in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjl421305s5\">5</a>. We adopt a concordance \u039bCDM cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m0</sub> = 0.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b0</sub> = 0.7, and <em>h</em> = 0.7. With these parameters, 1 arcsec corresponds to a physical scale of 5.76\u00a0kpc at the cluster redshift (<em>z</em> = 0.45; Allen et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r1\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r1\">2008</a>), and 5.62\u00a0kpc at <em>z</em> = 6.18.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl421305s2\" name=\"apjl421305s2\">2.\u00a0OBSERVATIONS AND REDSHIFTS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>MACS0329 was observed as part of CLASH with <em>HST</em> from 2011 August to 2011 October. This is one of 25 clusters to be observed to a total depth of 20 <em>HST</em> orbits in 16 filters with the Wide-Field Camera 3 (WFC3) UVIS and IR cameras, and the Advanced Camera for Surveys (ACS) WFC. The images are reduced and mosaicked (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />065 pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>) using standard techniques implemented in the <tt>MosaicDrizzle</tt> pipeline (Koekemoer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r30\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r30\">2002</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r30a\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r30a\">2011</a>). <em>HST</em> photometry for the arcs is obtained within the apertures shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f2\">2</a>, and photometric redshifts are estimated for all the galaxies in the field using the full 16-band UVIS/ACS/WFC3-IR aperture-matched photometry via both the BPZ (Ben\u00edtez <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r3\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r3\">2000</a>; Ben\u00edtez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r4\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r4\">2004</a>; Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r15\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r15\">2006</a>) and LePhare (Arnouts et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r2\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r2\">1999</a>; Ilbert et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r27\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r27\">2006</a>) programs. See Postman et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r39\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r39\">2012</a>) for additional details.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl421305f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl421305f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Thumbnails (5'' <b>&#x00d7;</b> 5'') of the most magnified arc of the <em>z</em> = 6.18 source (image 1.2) in different band-weighted-average combinations, with the aperture used for the photometry overlaid. As is clear, it is not seen below the F814W band, in agreement with the photometric redshift estimate. See Figure <a href=\"#apjl421305f3\">3</a> and Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjl421305t1\">1</a> for the SED and photometry, respectively.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjl421305f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadFigure/figure/apjl421305f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl421305f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl421305f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We supplement these <em>HST</em> observations with Infrared Array Camera (IRAC) imaging obtained in 2011 October as part of the <em>Spitzer</em> Cycle 8 warm mission (PI: R. Bouwens; see also Postman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r39\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r39\">2012</a>). The Warm <em>Spitzer</em> IRAC observations in Channels 1 and 2 (3.6 and 4.5\u2009\u03bcm) have a total integration time of 13, 290 s, and clearly detect three of the four images of the background source we report here (1.1\u20131.3), with a formal ~2\u03c3 detection for arc 1.4. Because of crowding in the <em>Spitzer</em> images, we adopt a circular 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />4 diameter aperture for the IRAC photometry. Background levels are estimated by sampling non-crowded sections of the IRAC mosaic while avoiding nearby bright sources. The accuracy of this (manual) photometry is verified by subtracting possible contaminating sources with GALFIT,<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjl421305fn1\">19</a></sup> especially for arc 1.2 which has a bright star nearby. We use a flux aperture correction factor of 1.9 <b>&#x00d7;</b>, based on a curve of growth analysis of unresolved sources in the Post Basic Calibrated Data mosaic. The relevant multi-wavelength photometry is given in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjl421305t1\">1</a> (see also Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f3\">3</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl421305f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl421305f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0SED modeling results of arc 1.2, the most magnified image of the <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 6.18 galaxy. The upper panel shows the observed and rest-frame SED and the maximum likelihood model fit. The filled red points indicate bands in which the object is well detected, while the open blue triangles indicate 2\u03c3 upper\u00a0limits; the open squares show the photometry of the best-fitting model convolved with the WFC3, ACS, and IRAC filter response functions. The open red circle indicates a spurious, marginally significant detection of arc 1.2 in the F606W band; however, we emphasize that none of the other images are detected in this band. We also show an inset with the photometric redshift distribution, <em>P</em>(<em>z</em>), obtained by combining the independent photometric redshift measurements of the four arcs, yielding a source redshift of <em>z</em> = 6.18<sup>+0.05</sup><sub>\u2212 0.07</sub> with BPZ, and 6.18<sup>+0.11</sup><sub>\u2212 0.13</sub> with LPZ (95% confidence levels). The lower panels show the posterior distributions on the demagnified stellar mass, SFR-weighted age, stellar metallicity (relative to <em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub> = 0.019), rest <em>V</em>-band dust attenuation, demagnified SFR, and specific SFR, sSFR\u2261SFR/<span class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn7.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathcal {M}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathcal {M}</script></span></span>. The vertical dashed lines show the median of each posterior distribution. We summarize the results in Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjl421305s4\">4</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl421305f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl421305f3\"><span rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\"pm\">26.42 \u00b1 0.13</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\"pm\">26.28 \u00b1 0.13</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\"pm\">24.8 \u00b1 0.2</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">&gt;24.9 (2\u03c3)</td></tr></tbody></table><p><small>\n<strong>Notes.</strong> Top: columns are: arc ID; R.A. and decl.; photo-<em>z</em> using BPZ and LePhare (hereafter LPZ), respectively;\u2009\u03bc, magnification predicted by the mass model. Bottom: multiband photometry for the dropout band (F775W) and all redder bandpasses, for the four images of the <em>z</em> = 6.18 galaxy, in AB magnitudes. Lower (2\u03c3)\u00a0limits are given for non-detections; we find no 2\u03c3 detections in any of the eight bluer bands. Note also that the (relative) magnitudes between the different images of this system agree overall with the (relative) magnifications derived by our mass model (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjl421305s4\">4</a>), with some deviation for the less magnified images, 1.3(1.4), which seem slightly less(more) magnified than our model implies.</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/suppdata/apjl421305t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/2041-8205/747/1/L9\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/suppdata/apjl421305t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl421305s3\" name=\"apjl421305s3\">3.\u00a0STRONG-LENSING MODELING AND ANALYSIS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The lens modeling method used here (e.g., Broadhurst et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r12\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r12\">2005</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r48\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r48\">2009</a>) begins with the assumption that mass approximately traces light. We model the distribution of cluster mass by assigning a power-law mass profile to each red-sequence cluster galaxy, scaled by its (relative) brightness. The sum of all galaxy contributions represents the lumpy galaxy component, which is then smoothed using two-dimensional spline interpolation to obtain a smooth component representing the dark matter (DM) distribution. The polynomial degree of smoothing and the index of the power law are the most important free parameters determining the mass profile.</p><p>A worthwhile improvement in fitting the location of the lensed images is generally found by introducing an external shear describing the overall matter ellipticity. The direction of the shear and its amplitude are free parameters, allowing for some flexibility in the relation between the distribution of DM and the distribution of galaxies. The weight of the lumpy component relative to the DM, and the overall normalization, bring the total number of free parameters in our modeling to six (see Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r48\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r48\">2009</a>).</p><p>The best fit is assessed by a \u03c7<sup>2</sup> minimization in the image plane, which is preferred because it generally does not produce solutions that are biased toward shallow mass profiles (and high magnifications), as is the case with source-plane minimization. The positions and morphologies of the multiply imaged arcs are accurately reproduced by the best-fit mass model in their measured photometric redshifts (for a morphological comparison example, see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f4\">4</a>), and the model is successively refined as additional sets of multiple images are incorporated.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl421305f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl421305f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Reproduction of system 1 by our model (lower row), compared with the real images (upper row). We delens image 1.1 to the source plane and relens it back to the image plane to reproduce the other images of this system. As can be seen, our model reproduces well the images of this system. Note also that our model requires larger deflection angles for the <em>z</em> = 6.18 source, relative to lower-<em>z</em> systems such as systems 2 and 3, independently strengthening its detection as a high-redshift source.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjl421305f4\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadFigure/figure/apjl421305f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl421305f4\" href=\"/2041-8205/747/1/L9/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl421305f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl421305s4\" name=\"apjl421305s4\">4.\u00a0RESULTS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We uncovered in <em>HST</em>/CLASH and <em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC imaging of MACS0329 one of the highest-redshift multiply lensed galaxies known to date. We combine the independent photometric-redshift distributions of its four lensed images to obtain a source redshift (and 2\u03c3\u00a0limits, see Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjl421305t1\">1</a>) of <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> = 6.18<sup>+0.05</sup><sub>\u2212 0.07</sub>. Using our mass model and the extensive imaging and resulting photometric redshifts, we physically matched 15 additional new multiple images and candidates of five background, lower-<em>z</em> sources (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f1\">1</a>), which are used in turn to refine the mass model. Explicitly, in addition to the four images of the high-<em>z</em> galaxy, we use as additional constraints the seven multiple images of systems 2 and 3, at photometric redshifts (and 2\u03c3\u00a0limits) of <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 2.17<sup>+0.12</sup><sub>\u2212 0.03</sub> and <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 2.89<sup>+0.05</sup><sub>\u2212 0.05</sub>, respectively, and verify that all other systems and candidates are plausible in the context of the resulting mass model.</p><p>The magnification by the cluster is coupled to the surface-density gradient in each point (i.e., the mass profile), so multiple systems with redshift information are important to assess the true magnification across the cluster field. For the four images of the <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> = 6.18 galaxy, we obtain magnifications (and 1\u03c3 uncertainties) of 11.6<sup>+8.9</sup><sub>\u2212 4.1</sub>, 17.6<sup>+6.2</sup><sub>\u2212 3.9</sub>, 3.9<sup>+3.0</sup><sub>\u2212 1.7</sub>, and 3.7<sup>+1.3</sup><sub>\u2212 0.2</sub>, respectively, so that in total the galaxy is magnified by a factor of <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 37.</p><p>We leverage the magnification boost of the most magnified image, arc 1.2, to construct a high-resolution image of the background galaxy, which occupies a source-plane area of ~2.2\u00a0kpc<sup>2</sup> (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f1\">1</a>). To further constrain the physical properties of this galaxy, we model the observed SED of arc 1.2 using the Bayesian SED-fitting code <tt>iSEDfit</tt> (see Moustakas et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r37\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r37\">2011</a>) coupled to the flexible stellar population synthesis models of Conroy et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r16\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r16\">2009</a>). We adopt the Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r14\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r14\">2003</a>) initial mass function from <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn3.gif\" alt=\"$0.1\\hbox{ to }100 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0.1\\hbox{ to }100 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>, assume the Calzetti et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r13\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r13\">2000</a>) dust attenuation law, and adopt uniform priors (based on Monte Carlo draws) on the stellar metallicity (0.0002 &lt; <em>Z</em> &lt; 0.03), <em>V</em>-band attenuation (0 &lt; <em>A<sub>V</sub></em> &lt; 2\u00a0mag), and galaxy age (0.005\u20131\u00a0Gyr). For reference, the age of the universe at <em>z</em> = 6.18 is 0.9\u00a0Gyr. We parameterize the star formation history \u03c8(<em>t</em>) as an exponentially declining function of time, <em>t</em>, given by \u03c8(<em>t</em>)\u221dexp\u2009(\u2212 <em>t</em>/\u03c4), where \u03c4 is the characteristic time for star formation. We draw \u03c4 from a uniform distribution between 0.01\u2009and\u20095\u00a0Gyr, which spans the range from passively evolving to continuous star formation.</p><p>In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f3\">3</a> we show the observed and rest-frame SED of arc 1.2, the maximum likelihood model fit, and the posterior distributions on all the model parameters. Adopting the median of each posterior distribution as our best estimate of the properties of the galaxy, we find a demagnified stellar mass of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"${\\sim}10^{9} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sim}10^{9} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>, low dust content (<em>A<sub>V</sub></em> ~ 0.1\u00a0mag), a demagnified SFR of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn5.gif\" alt=\"${\\sim}3.2 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sim}3.2 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>, and an SFR-weighted age of ~180\u00a0Myr. These results imply a specific SFR, sSFR \u2261 SFR/<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn6.gif\" alt=\"$\\mathcal {M}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\mathcal {M}</script></span></span>, of ~3.4\u00a0Gyr<sup>\u22121</sup>, corresponding to a mass-doubling time of just 600\u00a0Myr (assuming a 50% return fraction). The stellar metallicity and \u03c4 parameter (not shown) are not particularly well constrained, although solutions with subsolar metallicity and \u03c4 <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/Gt.gif\" alt=\"Gt\" align=\"absmiddle\" /> 0\u00a0Gyr are generally favored; the median of the posterior distributions imply subsolar metallicity, <em>Z</em>/<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub> ~ 0.5, and \u03c4 ~ 2.4\u00a0Gyr.</p><p>We verified that performing our SED modeling on the other (less magnified) images yields overall similar results. The demagnified SED of arc 1.1 is nearly identical to that of arc 1.2, and therefore the posterior distributions of the physical quantities we derive are very similar to those shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f3\">3</a>; the median quantities all agree to well within 0.1 dex (\u00b150%). The demagnified F125W magnitude of arc 1.3(1.4), on the other hand, is 0.8 mag brighter(fainter) than arcs 1.1 and 1.2, although this discrepancy is well within the statistical uncertainties on the magnifications. Nevertheless, at face value the fainter two arcs imply a 0.3\u20130.4\u00a0dex larger stellar mass and SFR, 0.2\u20130.6\u00a0mag more dust attenuation, and a very similar age, 200\u00a0Myr. However, we emphasize that the posterior distributions on these quantities overlap significantly with those of arcs 1.1 and 1.2, and therefore these differences do not affect our conclusions about the nature of this object.</p><p>Note also that the center of emission in the 3.6\u2009\u03bcm image is slightly different from that of the 4.5\u2009\u03bcm image (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f2\">2</a>). Repeating the photometry on the two different centers, we find this offset may introduce uncertainty of ~0.3 mag in the IRAC photometry. The effect of possible contamination from bright neighbors was re-examined for both emission centers, and was found to be typically 0.4 mag. However, we importantly verified that these higher uncertainties have only a negligible (&lt;0.1 dex) effect on the resulting physical properties, as the fit is governed by the <em>HST</em> photometry.</p><p>Finally, we use our lens model to constrain the physical characteristics of MACS0329. For the <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 6.18 source, the critical curves enclose a relatively large area, with an effective Einstein radius of <em>r<sub>E</sub></em> = 33<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />9 \u00b1 3'' (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />195\u00a0kpc at <em>z<sub>l</sub></em> = 0.45), and a projected mass of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"$1.89^{+0.10}_{-0.06} \\times 10^{14} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1.89^{+0.10}_{-0.06} \\times 10^{14} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl421305f1\">1</a>). For the lower redshift of system 2, <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> = 2.17, the Einstein radius is <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 27<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />7, and the critical curve encloses a projected mass of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn9.gif\" alt=\"$1.40^{+0.09}_{-0.05} \\times 10^{14} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1.40^{+0.09}_{-0.05} \\times 10^{14} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>. For completeness, we measure the (total) mass profile slope, <em>d</em>log\u2009\u03a3/<em>d</em>log\u2009<em>r</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> \u22120.61<sup>+0.05</sup><sub>\u2212 0.1</sub> (in the range 1''\u201352'', or 6 <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> <em>r</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 300\u00a0kpc; about twice the Einstein radius for <em>z<sub>s</sub></em> ~ 2), typical of <em>relaxed</em> and well-concentrated lensing clusters (e.g., Broadhurst et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r12\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r12\">2005</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r48\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r48\">2009</a>), and in agreement with the fairly circularly symmetric X-ray contours centered on the Brightest Cluster Galaxy; (BCG; see Mann &amp; Ebeling <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r33\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r33\">2011</a>).</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl421305s5\" name=\"apjl421305s5\">5.\u00a0DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSIONS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The discovery of a high-redshift galaxy in the field of MACS0329 adds to several known high-redshift galaxies lensed by galaxy clusters (e.g., Egami et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r20\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r20\">2005</a>; Bradley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r10\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r10\">2008</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r11\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r11\">2011</a>; Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r44\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r44\">2009</a>; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r40\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r40\">2011</a>). Here we summarize the properties of this unique source.\n</p><ul class=\"clear-list wd-inline-list\"><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">1.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">It is one of the highest-redshift multiply lensed objects known to date, and lensed into four separate images. The angular separation between arcs 1.2 and 1.4 is ~1', considerably larger than previously reported cases (Egami et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r20\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r20\">2005</a>; Richard et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r40\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r40\">2011</a>).</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">2.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">The source is one of the brightest at <em>z</em> &gt; 6: its <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>\u00a0magnitude is 24.0 AB, making it a viable candidate for follow-up spectroscopy.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">3.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">The galaxy is consistent with being a dwarf galaxy. Its intrinsic (delensed) magnitude of <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> = 27.1 AB makes it a sub-<em>L</em><sub>*</sub> galaxy at this redshift. It occupies a source-plane area of ~2.2\u00a0kpc<sup>2</sup>, similar to previously deduced sizes of high-<em>z</em> lensed galaxies (e.g., Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r46\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r46\">2011b</a>). Due to the hierarchical growth of structure, galaxies are expected to be small at high redshifts, with dwarf galaxies constituting the building material of larger structures. Our source-plane reconstruction shows at least three (possibly star-forming) knots, consistent with several other reports of high-redshift galaxies with multiple components (Franx et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r22\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r22\">1997</a>; Bradley et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r10\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r10\">2008</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r11\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r11\">2011</a>; Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r44\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r44\">2009</a>; Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r38\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r38\">2010</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r46\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r46\">2011b</a>), possibly as the result of merging. In addition, we measure an overall half-light radius of ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />12, consistent with that found in Bouwens et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r5\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r5\">2004</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r6\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r6\">2006</a>) and (Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r38\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r38\">2010</a>).</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">4.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">The SED fits to the multiband photometry of the source suggest a demagnified stellar mass of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn10.gif\" alt=\"${\\sim}10^{9} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sim}10^{9} \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>, an SFR-weighted age of ~180\u00a0Myr, subsolar metallicity (<em>Z</em>/<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub> ~ 0.5), low dust content (<em>A<sub>V</sub></em> ~ 0.1\u00a0mag), and a demagnified SFR of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/747/1/L9/Full/apjl421305ieqn11.gif\" alt=\"${\\sim}3.2 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\sim}3.2 \\,\\mathcal {M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>. The specific SFR of ~3.4\u00a0Gyr<sup>\u22121</sup>, which is slightly higher than that found by other recent studies (Gonzalez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r24\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r24\">2011</a>; Stark et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r42\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r42\">2009</a>; Labb\u00e9 et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r31\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r31\">2010</a>; McLure et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r35\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r35\">2011</a>), implies a mass-doubling time of just 600\u00a0Myr and therefore vigorous ongoing star formation considering its low mass.</div></li><li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"\" id=\"\">5.\u00a0\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\">The UV continuum is blue, with a UV slope \u03b2 = \u22122.5 \u00b1 0.06, consistent with measurements of other faint <em>z</em> ~ 6 galaxies and suggests that these sources are largely dust free (Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r8\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r8\">2009b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r9\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r9\">2011</a>; Finkelstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r21\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r21\">2011</a>; Vanzella et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl421305r43\" id=\"fnref-apjl421305r43\">2011</a>).The discovery of the galaxy presented here shows once more the novelty and tremendous potential of galaxy clusters for observationally accessing the faint early universe.</div></li></ul></div><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The authors thank Saurabh Jha for useful discussions, and the anonymous referee for valuable comments. The CLASH Multi-Cycle Treasury Program (GO-12065) is based on observations made with the NASA/ESA <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em>. The Space Telescope Science Institute is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc. under NASA contract NAS 5-26555. This work is based in part on observations made with the <em>Spitzer Space Telescope</em>, which is operated by the Jet Propulsion Laboratory, California Institute of Technology under a contract with NASA. Support for this work was provided by NASA through an award issued by JPL/Caltech. We thank the hospitality of Institut f\u00fcr Theoretische Astrophysik, Universit\u00e4t Heidelberg, where part of this work took place, and the Baden-W\u00fcerttemberg Stiftung.</p></div></div><!--            <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">CLASH: DISCOVERY OF A BRIGHT <I>z</I> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" /> 6.2 DWARF GALAXY QUADRUPLY LENSED BY MACS J0329.6-0211</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">A. class=\"replica-h4\">Keywords</div>\n\t\t<p><a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=11%2F50&amp;code_desc=dark+matter\">dark matter</a>; <a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=11%2F6&amp;code_desc=galaxies%3A+clusters%3A+general\">galaxies: clusters: general</a>; <a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=11%2F7&amp;code_desc=galaxies%3A+clusters%3A+individual\">galaxies: clusters: individual</a><a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_sub&amp;code=11%2F7&amp;code_desc=galaxies%3A+clusters%3A+individual&amp;subkwd=MACS_J0329_6_0211&amp;subkwd_desc=MACS+J0329.6-0211\">\n\t\t\t\t(MACS J0329.6-0211)\n\t\t\t</a>; <a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=11%2F18&amp;code_desc=galaxies%3A+high-redshift\">galaxies: high-redshift</a>; <a href=\"/searchaaskeyword?source=aas&amp;type=kwd_group&amp;code=2%2F46&amp;code_desc=gravitational+lensing%3A+strong\">gravitational lensing: strong</a></p>\n\t</div>\n<!-- Start Reprint Link
